Annex 1A
Monitoring and Evaluation Indicators
Since resources for TA activities can easily be wasted, it is essential to have a set of performance indicators through which the
Project Monitoring and Evaluation process will, in a timely way, (a) impose continuous discipline on the Project's
implementing parties, (b) facilitate refinement of the design if necessary at mid-term, and (c) provide a fair basis for final
evaluation. Indicators are needed to measure both outputs and their development impact on the one hand, and inputs and the
process towards achieving that impact on the other. In the case of this Project, the inputs are component-specific, while the
impact is a mixture of component-specific outputs and results that will be attributable to the combination of all the
components.
Taking the combination first, progress on achieving the broad Project objective of sustainable export growth, especially
through diversification, will be measured by three sets of indicators against FY99 baseline data which will be established by
the PCU and agreed with IDA within three months of the consultants' mobilization about the beginning of FY00:
(1)     Increased national growth rate of exports and their share of GDP - indicating more strongly export-led
growth. This "framework indicator" is needed if only as a point of reference to help assure that narrower goals are not being
achieved by diverting resources at the expense of overall export growth 3 It will require careful qualitative analysis rather
than simple achievement of predetermined numeric targets, since a variety of exogenous factors may enhance or retard the
Project's own impact. The analysis will need to control for such factors as unexpected shocks like floods and external market
changes as well as for exchange management or trade policy changes on which the Project may have only indirect if any
influence. Moreover, the improvements that may be attributable to the Project, especially to its learning curve dimension,
may be measurable only towards its closure and especially in subsequent years, when unassisted firms will follow examples
pioneered in the MGF subproject or take advantage of the improved operating environment.
(2)    Reduced national dependence on a narrow range of export products and markets - indicating diversification.
This can be measured more easily, since it relates more closely to specific Project activities, especially its large MGF
subproject. The expected product and market diversification will be measured broadly by changes in their respective "Gini"
concentration coefficients, and more specifically by comparing the export growth rates from particular industries with large
and small export shares in the base year (e.g. knitwear v. horticultural products).
(3)     Reduced national export dependence on imported inputs- indicating enhanced value added. This also relates
fairly closely to specific Project activities, especially the help for indirect and partial exporters in the Customs subproject. Like
the concentration measures, the value added ratios need to be measured and assessed at the industry level, since increases in
ihem are desirable only if they do not occur at the expense of quantity or quality.
The direct impact of the matching grant subproject will be assessed mainly in terms of observable changes in assisted firms'
capacity to expand exports in future, without assistance. Surveys at the beginning, middle and end of the Project period will
include comprehensive site visits to a minimum of 10% of grant recipients and a control group of similar firms not assisted by the
facility, and be supplemnented by data on all recipients retained by the management contractor. The evaluation will seek also to
gather some information on indirect impact on unassisted firms.4 The detailed performance indicators will be agreed with IDA
following the contractor's mobilization but could include the following four sets:
(4)     Increased exports by the assisted firms. The surveys will ascertain. (a) the achievement of an average annual
export performance equivalent to a multiple of the cost of the grants paid to thie firms, and (b) a larger increase in exports
among firms in the program as compared to the control group.
(5)     Competitiveness improvements in the assisted firms. The surveys will compare competitiveness indicators of
assisted firms with those of the control group, including production costs, workforce skill levels, other productivity indicators,
and market share. Other indicators will include adoption of new management processes such as export programming, new
distribution channels, launch of new products, and use of consultants for problem solving.
3 Even the broad objective of export-led growth is not an unqualified proxy for poverty reduction, since exports should not be favored at
the expense of highly efficient import replacement or non-traded activities
4 The "demonstration effect" of assisting some firms on others is not expected to be measurable even at the end of the three-year period
This should be examined in subsequenit surveys, however.



Project Appraisal Document                                                                             Page 29
Country: Bangladesh                                                            Project Title: Export Diversification Project
(6)    Quality improvements in the assisted firms. The surveys will compare indicators of product quality improvement
among assisted firms and the control group such as quality certifications (including ISO-9000), value increases, and rejection
rate decreases.
(7)    Export-oriented behavioral features. The surveys will inquire into customer orientation, institutionalization of
quality assurance and continuing product development, employee motivation, and company image. They will also specifically seek to
evaluate the willingness of firms to continue using specialist services but at full market prices.
In addition to such results indicators, performance will be monitored at the process level. As part of its contract, the
management contractor will develop and obtain MGF Board approval of an annual work plan for each twelve-month period of
operation of the contract. The plan will specify in detail the activities to be carried out in order to launch and promote the scheme,
and to manage it under the terms of the approved Statement of Policies & Operating Procedures. It will also specify the man-day
inputs for each activity. Progress made in achieving the plan targets, plus proposed modifications, would be reported to the Board
within 10 days of the end of each operational calendar quarter. The report should include data on: each application received, value
plus one paragraph describing the activity; each applications approved, value plus one paragraph on expected impact;
each applications rejected, one paragraph describing reasons; breakdown of approvals by subsector, size of firm, and type of
grant; number of site visits; number and value of disbursements and time elapsed after authorization; and
project implementation issues. The value of grants approved resulting from the contractor's promotional and appraisal work
is expected to reach US$4 million in each fiscal year. The contractor is also expected to gather and compile infonnation which
would assist the impact evaluations discussed above
The impact of the Customs subproject will be measured in terms of indicators specific to its various components,
(8)    Customs service delivery improvements. Streamlining export procedures (Component 1) and piloting more
fundamental departures from transactions-based assessment (Component 5) should facilitate trade. Specific FY99
benchmarks and expectations for FY0O-02 in this regard will be developed by the Consultants and agreed with NBR/IDA
shortly after mobilization.5 They are expected to measure changes, compared with FY99, in such variables as: (a) cost of
complying with Customs procedures in terms of facilitation payments, sales lost or costs increased by clearance delays, etc.;
(b) the cost-effectiveness of services provided, elapsed time for various key procedures, and number of disputes; (c) ratio of
legal to illegal imports, with a methodology for this to be developed with help from the PATC and PCU advisory teams; and
(d) client satisfaction, especially on the part of exporters, to be determined by surveys. They shall include the following
quantitative indicators which were agreed with NBR at Negotiations:

(9)    Improved Customs/NBR information systems. Successful implementation of the proposed new Customs data and
management information systems (Component 2) will be assessed through the following indicators: (a) Y2k problems averted
within 1999; (b) unique TIN applied to all Customs transactions within by June 2000; (c) ASYCUDA++ or similar system
operational by December 2000; (d) satisfactory performance of other MIS systems by that date, with (e) further improvement
in 2001. Specific benchmarks and expectations for the MIS will be developed by the Consultants and agreed with NBR/IDA
shortly after mobilization.
(10)   Liberalised bonded warehouse scheme. Successful implementation of the proposed SBW monitoring system
(Component 3) will be assessed through the following indicators: (a) new system operational for existing licensees by June
2000; (b) no potential SBW applicant being considered "too hard to monitor" by June 2001, enabling (c) new rules to be
promulgated and effective by that date to open the system to partial exporters in most industries.
(11)    Expanded duty drawback scheme. Successful implementation of the proposed expansion of the DD scheme
(Component 4) will be assessed through the following indicators: (a) flat rates available for 50% of major domestic inputs by
June 2000; and (b) Cash Compensation Scheme phased out by June 2001, with all indirect exporters being well served by
DEDO.

Apart from these results indicators, performance monitoring will occur at the process level with respect to the work plan
which the subproject team will develop and have endorsed by NBR management shortly after mobilization of the contractor's
team members. An illustrative example of such a plan for the major Component 5 is included in Annex 2D below for
reference. Progress on implementing the approved plan and any proposed modifications should be discussed among the
subproject team, NBR management and the PCU on the basis of a progress report to be provided by the team within 10 days of
the end of each operational calendar quarter.
Unless the capacity building vrotection analysis and trade cooperation subproject is paralleled rather than followed by trade
liberalization, its economic impact will be felt only beyond the Project period. Accordingly the performance indicators will
relate mainly to the process of capacity building, viz:
(12)    Technical staff training in trade policy analysis. Success in this area will be measured by the number of staff
proficient in ERP analysis: 4 by June 2000, 8 by June 2001; all retained or adequately replaced by June 2002.
(13)   Technical staff training in trade cooperation. Similarly, success here will depend on thew number of staff
proficient in rules, procedures and/or economics of incurring, monitoring and enforcing trade treaty obligations: 4 by June
2000, 8 by June 2001; all retained or adequately replaced by June 2002.
(14)   Processes for ensuring balanced analysis. Performance will be measured by: (a) the number of high quality (peer
reviewed) analytical studies on subsectors or themes: at least 4 per year including one overview of protection; and (b) the
number of well conducted public hearings with broad participation of affected interests: at least 4 per year.
(15)   Sustainability of capacity built by the subproject. Sustainability will be judged by: (a) a satisfactory system and
rules in place by June 2001 to ensure retention or appropriate replacement of technically trained staff in MOC and BTC; (b)
the appointment of high caliber BTC Members with appropriate experience when present Members are replaced; and (c)
substantial improvement in the autonomy and authority of the BTC as an organization: institutional review completed by June
2000, satisfactory reorganization plan approved by December 2000, and fully implemented by June 200 1.
With respect to process indicators, this subproject will have arrangements similar to those noted above for Customs, but with
MOC and BTC as the joint endorsing authority and with the plan covering both IDA/BDXDP- and DFID/TPCBP-financed
activities.
The scope of the coordination and development subproject is divided between project management functions and analytical
aspects of export promotion. Two sets of success indicators are prescribed for eachi of these aspects:
(16)   Project monitoring. The PCU's performance in this area will be evaluated in terms of the quality of (a) the analysis
it undertakes to establish quantitative benchmarks and to measure progress against them; (b) its regular progress reports on
all the subprojects' inputs and outputs; and (c) the surveys of user satisfaction which it will conduct in cooperation with MGF,
Customs and PATC subproject teams.
(17)   Project accounts. The Unit's performance in this area will be certified by the independent audit's findings with
respect to timeliness, accuracy, and methodological consistency with LACI and COSTAB.
(18)   Institutional development analysis. Performance will be judged by the annual completion of at least two
satisfactory major studies on such topics as BTC, MOC, quota monitoring, and institutions for accreditation, certification and
standards. One of the second year's studies should produce satisfactory proposals on the reorganization of the EPB, role of
business organizations in export promotion, and institutionalization of the PCU's own work.
(19)    Export constraints analysis. Performance will be judged by the annual completion of (a) at least two satisfactory
major studies on such topics as export finance/guarantee, port/factory transport logistics, international air/sea freight services,
other infrastructure, standards issues, etc. -- one of whiclh may be a compilation of several minor topics; and (b) at least two
thoroughly prepared subproject proposals or investment prefeasibility studies - one of which may be a compilation of
summary proposals for donors (e.g the IF Round Table in 1999).
With respect to process indicators, this subproject will have arrangements similar to those noted above for Customs, but with
MOC as the endorsing authority.

The product and market development support (PMDS) component comprises funding of a Matching Grant Facility, one
major TA subproject to manage the Facility, and several other subprojects to be developed during Project implementation. It
addresses a number of market failures which hold back the rate at whiclh exporters in Bangladesh can exploit their
comparative advantage in the international marketplace. These include lack of awareness of the types of services that can
assist exporters, lack of knowledge on how to access these services from abroad and locally, and the perceived high costs of
these services by exporters. There has also been little development of local services to help firms build export
competitiveness. Examples of services to be supported by the Project are those that help diversify exports through product
improvement or development and expansion of export markets. Specific activities include advisory services, quality
improvement initiatives, management and staff training, marketing research and exploration trips, product testing, and
shipping of samples. Provision of these services will be market-based and tailored to specific needs of exporters or groups of
exporters. In addition, the Project Component will encourage local service providers to speed up the development of local
business support services Examples of the types of such services to be supported include travel to develop joint ventures
with foreign specialist firms, training staff, and bringing in short-term foreign specialist to help build new services.
I (a) and (b) Matching Grant Facility
($28.46 million including $15.80 million IDA)
(a) Grants for private firms and groups' PMD initiatives and for service providers ($24 million of which $12 million
paid by participating firms and $12 million by IDA).- The MGF is a temporary instrument to encourage in an active
manner the use of business support services to enhance finns' export capabilities by providing grants covering 50% of the
cost of service fees and associated travel expenses. Grants can be made either to exporters acquiring services or to firns
gearing up to provide them. Eligible initiatives will include any activity which will build export competitiveness, e.g. quality
itmprovement initiatives, testing and certification of process and product, enterprise training focused on export needs,
technical assistance to help with product adaptation and market identification and development.
Key characteristics (see the Statentent of Policies and Operating Procedures, Annex 2A, forfurther detail)
.  Basic criteria: The MGF will provide quick disbursing grants on a 50:50 basis, expected to be committed within a three
year period. Grants are intended for (i) individual firms or small groups thereof as service-users, and (ii) private firms,
NGOs or associations as service-providers. It is expected that individual service users will form the majority of
beneficiaries. "Deemed exporters" supplying products within Bangladesh are eligible if they (will) supply goods or
services to direct exporters.
*  Exceptions to the 5050 rule will be strictly "ring-fenced": There will be no exceptions for exporters, and the general
rule for export support services requiring more than 50% and/or receiving other public funding is to appraise them as
separate subprojects outside the MGF -- see 1 (c) etc below
*  Conflict of interest rules: Any beneficiary of matching or non matching grant funding cannot be involved in MGF
supervision or otherwise associated with it. Firms associated with the management contractor may not be beneficiaries,
and Board members will declare and excuse themselves from cases involving industries in wilch they have any interest.
. Maximnum grant size: No single industry will receive more than 20% of total grant funds. For this purpose "industry"
may be defined as, for example, knitwear, furniture, frozen fish, woven RMG. No single firm within an industry may
receive more than $200,000. The MGF Board and IDA may review these caps from time to time.
* Basic firm eligibility: Grants are not intended to relieve financial distress, so currently "sick" enterprises would need
recovery plans that would enable any MGF-created or -identified opportunities to be exploited. Similarly, firms not in
compliance with Bangladesh's labor or environmental laws need to have firm plans to correct their status.
*  Eligible activities: Any business support services determined by an individual firm to support export diversification is
eligible. While the facility will not finance capital investment, it could assist preparation of bankable projects.
* Available funds: The allocation is based on the Estinmated Demandfor the Matching Grant Facility (Annex 2B).



Project Appraisal Document                                                                            Page 32
Country: Bangladesh                                                            Project Title: Export Diversification Project
(b) MGF administration and advisory services (S4.46 million including $3.8 million IDA).- The MGF will be
administered by a Board and a professional management team under contract for the duration of the Project. The team will
be fielded by the Trade Development Institute of Ireland, which [has been] appointed through a competitive bidding process.
Contract implementation will include the provision of advisory and administration services for three market-building
interventions: (i) active promotion to the private sector of the benefits of utilizing support services to diversify exports, (ii)
on-going hand-holding advice on the process, development of grant requests, and identification of service providers, and (iii)
administration of the matching grants to exporters and service providers The management team also will contribute to
constraints identification and analysis under Subproject 2 (c) below.
Management team:
International consultants:
* MGF manager = Senior technical advisor (STA/team leader), 36 months
* Deputy manager/controller (initial period), 16 months
* Export development advisors, several totaling 24 months
* Headquarters back-up services, equivalent to 6 months                   (Subtotal international: 82 months)
Local consultants:
* Deputy manager, 20 months following understudy period 16 months
. Export development advisors, several totaling 48 months                 (Subtotal local: 84 months)
Support staff.
Key characteristics:
. Administration of the MGF. The fund will be administered jointly by: (i) a seven member MGF Supervisory Board
composed of public and private representatives, and (ii) the contracted MGF management team funded by IDA. The
contractor will operate the fund under Annual Operating Plans by accepting, evaluating, and approving (delegated
categories of) grant applications subject to Board oversight, and maintaining performance and financial records.
* Establishment offund management. The Board will adopt the Statement of Policies and Operating Procedures (SPOP,
see Annex 2A) and [has participated] in the contracting process initiated during project appraisal, in preparation for
implementation as soon after IDA Credit effectiveness as possible.
. Board responsibility The Board will be responsible for reviewing and approving Annual Operating Plans submitted by
the contractor, and supervising the operation of the scheme through these annual plans and through Quarterly Operating
Reports submitted by the contractor, comparing actual performance with planned.
. Approval process. The MGF approval process, while conforming with GOB and IDA accounting requirements, will be
designed to be swift disbursing by applying prescribed transparent criteria announced publicly by the Board through the
SPOP. Approval of applications will be granted either at Board meetings, by "no objection" on circulated files, or by
delegation to the Unit The Board will thoroughly monitor performance, on an ex post basis.
I (c) etc. Other PMD Subprojects
(Initial allocation $1.27 million including $1.0 million IDA)
These activities are to be identified and developed during Project implementation, mainly by the Project Coordination and
Development Unit in the course of its constraints and institutional analyses (see Subproject 2 (c) below) but with active
contributions from the MGF team and other Project staff They could include support for public, private or collective:
* accreditation, certification, standards, or testing services (e g. Department of Fisheries laboratory),
* quota and/or origin monitoring functions (e.g. MOC garment quota management in cooperation with BGMEA), and
* institutionalized enterprise training to improve quality/productivity (e.g certain skills of interest to various exporters).
Criteria for IDA/GOB approval of such subprojects will include their:
. expected direct contribution to the diversification of export products or markets or to incrcasing value added,
* complementarity with other project activities,
* focus on the development of sustainable capacity and expertise for supporting export production and/or marketing,
especially in the private sector or in areas requiring public/private cooperation, and/or
* strengthening of essential public capacity in trade management.
Consideration may be given also to providing project funds to support specified service or promotional activities by NGOs or
even private firms under arrangemnents not suitable for the MGF. These would be put out to tender and funded to an extent
determined by the bid from the firm or NGO able to perform the service for the lowest subsidy.

The trade management capacity building (TMCB) component comprises three subprojects. The largest will initiate GOB's
proposed Revenue Administration Modernization Programme (RAMP) by undertaking Phase I of Customs administration
modernization. This will remove one of the most important and costly impediments in the business environment for export
activity, and at the same time test new approaches that will later be generalized to improve efficiency and equity throughout
the revenue system -- to the benefit of all honest commerce as well as placing revenue collection on a sound administrative
base. One focus of the subproject will be on the mechanisms to reduce exporters' input costs through enclave free-trade
arrangements. This trade policy theme will be taken up more broadly in the second subproject, which will address two key
dimensions of exploiting the scope for faster economic growth througlh export production: Bangladesh's unilateral process of
trade liberalization; and its participation in global and regional arrangements for trade cooperation. Finally, a coordination
subproject will combine technical work on export constraints, including institutional development needs, with the facilitation
and monitoring of the rest of the Project and the development of new subprojects under Component 1 (c) etc.
2 (a) Customs Administration Modernization, Phase I
($9.61 million including $8.25 million IDA)
This subproject will represent the first major undertaking in the GOB's proposed Revenue Administration Modernization
Program (RAMP). As well as dealing with several important changes that are sharply focussed on improving the Customs
environment for export, the subproject will pilot various process, technology, culture and organizational changes that will
ultimately be implemented for all Customs and other tax assessment and collection. It contains five components to be
implemented with technical assistance provided by an experienced consulting firm, Clapp & Mayne, of the US, which [has
been] appointed through a competitive process to field a team of international and local experts. The team will also help
NBR with other subproject components, i.e. to acquire appropriate equipment, and to coordinate inputs from (a) fee-free
experts provided through the WCO, and (b) systems support which UNCTAD may need to provide to ensure successful
installation of ASYCUDA++.
Consulting team:
International consultants on:
*  Customs modernization = Senior teclnical advisor (team leader), 36 months
*  Information technology / ASYCUDA, 36 months
*  Information systems, 36 months
*  Customs risk management, 6 months
*  Customs audit policy and practice, 6 months
*  Customs bonded warehouse management, 6 months

Subproject components:
(I) Streamlined export and related-import clearance procedures.- The consultants and their NBR counterparts will design
and introduce fast-track procedures for the clearance of exports and of imports associated with exports (to pilot such
procedures for application to all imports in Phase II) Specific steps will include:
reviewing present operating procedures by Customs, other authorities (port, airport, security, etc.), and service providers



Project Appraisal Document                                                                           Page 34
Country: Bangladesh                                                           Project Title: Export Diversification Project
(carriers, local transport, container facilities, clearing agents, etc.) whichi affect the flow of goods during import/export;
* identifying changes in requirements, functions and relationships that would expedite the flows;
* designing, implementing, and closely monitoring a pilot scheme involving a significant proportion of exports and the
imports associated with them to test the new procedures; and
* identifying refinements that would be necessary to mainstream the fast track procedures.
(2) Installation of ASYCUDA++ and other MIS capacity.- The consultants and their NBR counterparts -- in cooperation
with UNCTAD or other provider of inputs under a separate contract -- will organize implementation of ASYCUDA "++" or
equivalent system to replace version "2.6/2,7", extending its scope to all Customs entry points, and taxpayer access. Specific
steps will include:
* reviewing, refining and gaining approval of the "A++" plan prepared for NBR in 1998;
* validating or correcting the present prescription, and arranging the procurement and installation of equipment;
* training operators in data capture, verification, and analysis techniques;
* managing the switches from "2.6" to "2.7" within 1999 at NBR and the Dhaka and Chittagong customshouses and NBR
HQ, and then to "A++" or similar system within 2000;
* managing extension to all import and export transactions;
* designing links with the data processing for other tax instruments (and perhaps with preshipment assessments);
*  designing reporting formats for "A++" or equivalent and other MIS (in consultation with BB, BTC, and other users);
* if applicable, arranging hand-over of "A++" maintenance to UNCTAD Kuala Lumpur (about July 2001); and
* ensuring smooth implementation of links and reporting mechanisms.
The other management information systems that NBR may require (apart from ASYCUDA or equivalent) are to be planned
in detail after mobilization of the team, building on the initiatives taken under the ETAC subproject of TA-VI.
(3) Improved special bonded warehouse scheme monitoring.- The consultants and their NBR counterparts will design and
introduce new monitoring procedures to make the bonding scheme relatively leakage-proof, and thus enable the more liberal
availability of the scheme to a wide range of industries including producers for both export and domestic markets. Specific
steps will include:
* reviewing in-depth the present operation of the scheme, including producers' dependence on proftts from leaked inputs
and products that evade CDVAT;
* designing a monitoring mechanism, linked to or based in the new ASYCUDA, that is not onerous for importer-exporters
but which tracks and relates imports, domestic purchases, domestic sales of inputs and goods (subject to CDVAT),
exports of goods, and re-exports of inputs;
* piloting the proposed mechanism on a selection of existing SBWs,
* justifying a policy change to issue SBW licenses to producers in any industry, including those intending to sell part of
their imported inputs and/or their products (rejects, etc ) legally in the domestic market, and recommending incentives
for them to do so;
* arranging equipment (if necessary),
* training staff and educating licensees' accountants in the new procedures; and
*  managing the first year of operation under the new licensing scheme and monitoring procedures.
(4) Improved duly drawback replacing cash compensation.- The consultants and DEDO staff will design and introduce new
procedures to facilitate (a) payment of CD, VAT and SD drawback immediately upon export slhipment, and (b) easy receipt
of drawback by indirect exporters. Specific steps will include:
* designing the new procedures;
*  designing the consequent changes in the computerization system including links or access to ASYCUDA, staff training,
and equipment upgrading requirements;
* introducing the new procedures on a pilot basis;
* justifying a policy change to dispense with the requirement for proceeds realization certificates (PRC) before payout;
* procuring equipment;
* training staff,
*  mainstreaming the new procedures; and
* justifying a policy change to replace the present cash compensation scheme (CCS) for fabric producers by the streamlined
access to drawback for indirect exporters.
(5) Piloting post-audit, risk-management, and other new methods/culture/structures.- The consultants and their NBR
counterparts, in cooperation with WCO and other advisors to NBR, will design, pilot, and plan the implementation of new
procedures and organizational arrangements due to be operationalised coimnencing by CY2002, and will prepare staff and
taxpayers for them through training and recruitment activities. Specific steps will include:
* designing procedures to implement the substantial replacement of transactions-based operations by ex post tax audits,



Project Appraisal Document                                                                            Page 35
Country: Bangladesh                                                           Project Title: Export Diversification Project
supported by sophisticated modem risk management techniques;
* indicating linkages and synergies among parallel changes in Customs and other tax administration (in cooperation with
the Modernization Group's VAT/Excise and Direct Tax Teams),
* review successful, relevant experience elsewhere in developing organizational arrangements conducive to efficient
Customs and other tax administration (e.g. Uganda's new Revenue Authority), and design an arrangement suitable for
Bangladesh;
. defining legislative changes that may be needed to authorize the new procedures and organization;
* defining staffing requirements for implementing them, including detailed plans for training, recruitment, restructuring,
and remuneration;
. building up-front political, bureaucratic, taxpayer, and staff consensus for the proposed changes, including through a first
batch of taxpayer education and staff training programs; and
. operating pilot programs to introduce new processes.
Specific outputs and their key performance indicators for this component (5) are shown in Annex 2D.
Training activities:
A substantial training program provisionally budgeted at $0.85 million will combine local on-the-job training, formal
courses and workshops for about 400 staff, and study tours and other foreign training for about one-third that number.
Topics range from ASYCUDA operation and other computer literacy to the more specialized subjects of risk management,
auditing, drawback systems and warehouse bonding. The separate memorandum of understanding with UNCTAD is
expected to cover part of the ASYCUDA requirements, while others will be facilitated by the main consulting team.
Equipment and works:
A $3.24 million budget provides mainly for electronic detection gear, computing and networking equipment, and site
renovation for housing the latter properly. Most of this expenditure may occur early in the subproject period to facilitate
both short- and medium-term measures to reduce rent-seeking and smuggling. Some could be delayed until ASYCUDA++
is installed in 2000, however, providing an opportunity for significant process changes to occur -- with the consultants' help
-- before ++-related equipment expenditures will be incurred. This should help ensure effective use of thie equipment.
2 (b) Protection Analysis and Trade Cooperation
($4.03 million including $3.30 m IDA & $0.85 m DFID parallel financing)
This subproject has two distinct major components addressing protection analysis and other support for tariff reform, and
global/regional trade cooperation, a supporting data management component, and a contribution to a reorganization study.
It will be located primarily in the Bangladesh Tariff Coimmission, but the trade cooperation component will also involve
systems and staff of the Ministry of Commerce The subproject will be implemented partly with parallel funding by the
United Kingdom's Department for International Development's Trade Policy Capacity Building Project, and perhaps with
fee-free experts on global trade cooperation provided through the World Trade Organization An experienced consulting
finn, Maxwell Stamp PLC, of the UK, [has been] appointed througlh a competitive process under IDA guidelines to help
MOC/BTC utilize and coordinate those resources as well as to field and supervise its own substantive inputs.
Consulting team
International consultants:
*  Senior technical advisor (STA/team leader), 36 months
*  Information system advisor, 15 months
.  Subsector analysts and trade cooperation advisors, several
totaling 29 months IDA + 1 1 months DFID *                   (Subtotal: 80 mnths IDA + 11 mnths DFID)
Local consultants:
.  Deputy technical advisor (DTA), 36 months
.  Information system advisor, 23 months including two-month
* overlap with international counterpart
*  Subsector analysts and trade cooperation advisors, several
totaling 42 months and 30 months DFID *                      (Subtotal: 101mnths IDA + 30 mnths DFID)
Support staff: Office assistants, drivers, etc
* The DFID consultants willfunction as part of the team, thouigh employed through a separate Project Management Agency.
Subproject components
(I) Trade policy analysis.- This component is intended to either complement and assist reforms that GOB may have
committed itself to under the PFP or to help induce them by raising the quality of protection measurement and analysis.
Studies, workshops, training programs and other activities will be undertaken to assist the transfer of knowledge and



Project Appraisal Document                                                                            Page 36
Country: Bangladesh                                                            Project Title: Export Diversification Project
development of skills in such areas as:
* monitoring the impact of trade liberalization on the economy as a whole and on selected industries, paying particular
attention to efficient resource allocation and employment;
* analyzing effective protection at the economy wide level and in subsectors such as textile machinery and spare parts and
other capital machinery and engineering industries, ceramic products, plastic products, electronics, jute and jute
products, toiletries and cosmetics, paper and paperboard, and artificial flowers;
*  conducting public hearings and applying other techniques for ensuring equitable policy formulation;
* dealing with anti-dumping, countervailing and other safeguard measures taken by export destination countries, and
considering the application of such measures against imports;
*  measuring anti-export bias in the tariff and QR structure, and servicing formal joint GOB/IDA/IMF reviews of the degree
and effects of such bias in trade policy;
* examining through protection analysis the appropriateness of various agreements for Bangladesh, especially the
implications of moving from SAPTA to SAFTA.
(2) Official trade cooperation.- This component will strengthen or create the capacities of BTC and MOC and skills of their
staff to handle trade cooperation arrangements at the bilateral, subregional, regional and multilateral levels, including (a)
monitoring the WTO agreements in order to derive full advantage of opportunities that have emerged from the Uruguay
Round of multilateral trade negotiations and to abide by its rules and disciplines and (b) identifying key areas for regional
cooperation with particular focus on export promotion. This will involve analytical and advisory work, integrated with on-
the-job and formal training activities staff, including:
* assisting with preparation of policy briefings for Ministers and the decision makers on WTO related negotiations and
bilateral, subregional, and regional trading arrangements;
* monitoring the UR Agreements and suggesting policy actions in order to derive full advantages of opportunities that have
emerged from the Round and to abide by its rules and obligations while maximizing the transfer of knowledge to the
officials of BTC and MOC so that they can handle the issues efficiently;
* assisting GOB in preparing full consultation report on Balance of Payments as required under WTO rules and in writing
the GOB report on Trade Policy Review for the WTO;
* arranging workshops, training and seminars on various issues of WTO, regional, and subregional agreements and on
new trade issues and overseeing the delivery of all necessary inputs, and
*  conducting studies on various Uruguay Round Agreements and on new trade issues, suggesting policy actions.
Apart from the safeguards topic noted in (1) above, the focus in global cooperation is expected to be on the agreements on
* agriculture,
* technical barriers to trade, and sanitary and phyto-sanitary regulations,
* textiles and clothing,
* trade in services, and in intellectual property.
(3) Information systems to support both trade policy analysis and trade cooperation.- This component will support the
others by developing a proper information services system so that the officials of BTC will have easy access to data needed to
formulate trade related policies and assist MOC in trade cooperation arrangements, and by establislhing linkage with other
national and international organizations in order to have quick access to information and data. This will involve:
* developing information service facilities in BTC for compilation, analysis and electronic data processing of trade,
industry, and other data for monitoring and policy analysis and for supporting trade cooperation function.
* developing a Management Information System in BTC, including assessing the need for data management
hardware/software and other required inputs and preparing documents for procurement of all necessary equipment;
* maintaining regular contract with other national and international organization (WTO/UNCTAD/ITC/EU) and
establishing linkages with other national and international agency for future work in trade policy areas, and
* establishing a resource centre in BTC to include copies of all consultancy and research reports produced under the
BDXDP as well as relevant publications and issues papers produced by WTO, UNCTAD and academic institutions.
(4) Institutional development of BTC and MOC.- In addition to their substantive tasks, the subproject staff will collaborate
with the PCU team in its proposed institutional analysis aimed at recommending structural changes, including in status and
staffing, needed to enhance these organizations' in-house technical capability and impact on trade policy and management.
Training, equipment and other expenses:
Apart from the consultancy components, budgetary provision has been made for one-year external courses for four staff,
short courses abroad for 15, local seminars, information service development, technical staff travel to Trade Cooperation
meetings, and computing and communication equipment and software

An Export Diversification Project Coordination and Development Unit (PCUJ), which may be institutionalized following the
Project period, will be responsible not only for facilitating and monitoring Project activities but also for identifyingl
analyzing constraints, advising on needs for institutional reorganization, and helping GOB develop new PMD subprojects
and activities for IDA Project or other funding. Its coordination function will be formalized through its leadership role in the
Technical Committee comprising the project directors and heads of the consulting teams for the MGF, CAM-1, PATC and
other subprojects. In addition it is represented on the MGF Board thirouglh both the PD for Coordination (= Additional
Secretary of Commerce) and the CTA (as a non-voting member). The Unit's own consulting staff will be fielded by an
experienced project management firm -- International Business and Teclnical Consultants Inc. of the US (in association
with Business and Government Strategies International of the US and Uniconsult International of Bangladesh) -- which [has
been] selected through competitive bidding under IDA guidelines.

Main activities
(1) Facilitating Project activities.- The Unit will play a dual role with respect to the other components of the Project. On the
one hand, it will facilitate them by providing coordination, accounting and procurement services and technical advice. On
the other, it will monitor their performance -- see (2) below  Specific facilitation and support services will include:
. ensuring the availability of funds by arranging timely replenishment of the Special Account;
* issuing cheques as required for payments authorized by subproject managements;
. providing accounting fornats and advice to subproject bookkeepers or, preferably, maintaining subproject financial
records on their behalf in LACI format,
  providing procurement guidelines and technical advice to subproject directors or preferably, on request, undertaking
procurement on their behalf;
* assisting subproject managements in logistic arrangements for visiting experts' arrival and departure, internal transport
arrangements, organization of workshops and seminars, access to data and local services, etc.
  advising on the suitability of proposed subproject training courses and candidate selection to achieve required subproject
human resource development objectives,
. providing peer review or other commentary on subproject technical reports;
(2) Monitoring and reporting on Project activities .- In monitoring Project and subproject performance and reporting to the
Steering Committee (representing GOB) and IDA, specific PCU activities will include, in cooperation with implementing
agencies and subproject managements:
 defining performance indicators (including export ratios and concentration indices for overall Project impact);
. verifying and consolidating subproject progress reports;
. undertaking the internal audit of subproject accounts;
* preparing any reports required by IDA in defined format;
* facilitating GOB participation in IDA supervision missions; and
* contributing to and facilitating the technical evaluation of subproject outputs;
The Unit's own facilitation activities -- see (1) above -- and substantive work -- see (3) - (6) below - will be subject to the
same monitoring and reporting process, all of which is subject to regular Teclmical Committee review, as well as mid-term
and end-of-Project impact analysis - see External Evaluation and Audit.
(3) Identifying/analyzing constraints.- A relatively small but very significant share of the Project's overall substantive work
will be undertaken by the PCU's own team - in collaboration with subproject staff where appropriate - comprising the

identification and analysis of export constraints with a view to proposing feasible solutions. Topics remain to be determined
and prioritized, and a work plan will be agreed soon after mobilization and reviewed by the Technical Committee on a
regular basis. It could include any significant constraints or sources of business cost-increases that may be categorized as:
* bottlenecks which could be removed through infrastructural investments, public or private, for which the PCU
contribution could include prefeasibility cost/benefit analysis; and
* delays or other costs which could be removed through policy or procedural changes, for which the PCU contribution
could include design and advocacy of measures which would retain or provide suitable substitutes for those aspects of
regulations with public policy justification.
(4) Advising on needs for institutional reorganization.- A key subset as well as a consequence of (3) will involve
institutional analysis, in order to help GOB and FBCCI determine and implement appropriate, demand-driven institutional
mechanisms to provide export support services in the public sector or as public/private entities. In some cases this will
involve the reform of existing entities which could provide better service if they are reorganized and/or strengthened.
Entities and issues that have been tentatively pre-identified for consideration include:
. Export Promotion Bureau may need private management, commercialization, and/or separation of regulatory and
promotion responsibilities;
. Bangladesh Tariff Commission may need greater autonomy and/or broader mandate to address competition issues;
* MOC's international trade organizations and SAARC units need legal ability to retain long-term technical staff; and
. Bangladesh Standards and Testing Institute and/or Bangladesh Council for Scientific and Industrial Research may need
reorganization to serve as accreditation agencies.
(5) Developing new PMD subproiects and activities - Based on its own analytical work and other identification activities,
the Unit will assist GOB agencies and private organizations to prepare subprojects, focussed on export product and market
development, which could be financed under subcomponent I (c) of the Project or by other sources. Topics which have been
raised for consideration in this regard include technical strengthening of:
. The garment quota management, rules-of-origin certification, and other such functions now performed by EPB; and
* The Department of Fisheries certification or accreditation capability
Other subprojects may be identified in consultation with the WTO/UNCTAD International Trade Centre, other sources of
technical assistance, and/or otlher multilateral and bilateral donors. The PCU is expected to play a key role in an important
interagency process for identifying specific activities potential lielpers and donors for suclh TA, namely the Integrated
Frameworkfor Trade Related TA to Least Developed Countries. In this connexion, it will assist MOC and sector Ministries
prepare for and (with IDA) organize a national Round Table early in the Project period as well as possible follow-up events.
(6) Planning its own succession.- The work which the PCU will undertake under (2) - (5) above should not cease at the end
of the three-year Project. Accordingly, an important function of the Unit, especially during the third year, will be to prepare
for such work to continue in (an) appropriate institutional setting(s). This may mean the transfer of its responsibilities to a
revitalized and reorganized Export Promotion Bureau, to an Exporters Association or export division of the FBCCI, or to a
new entity with shared public/private management.
