Annex 6
Procurement, Financial Management
and Disbursement Arrangements
A. Procurement
Major procurement under the project will be consultants' services, including training, and procurement of computer
hardware and software. There are several consultants' service contracts under the project of which processing of
four [has been] completed before Board presentation. The remaining consultants' services will be identified and
processed during implementation phase of the project. While indicative requirement of computers have been made,
the details will be worked out after the consultants, recruited under different contracts, make detailed
recommendations on the specifications and the number of units to be procured. The Procurement Plan, identifyilng
major contract packages including schedule, has been agreed and is annexed to the PIP.
Table 6.1 summarizes the project items, their related cost estimates and proposed methods of procurement. Table 6.2
summarizes the threshold for procurement methods and prior review Project-related procurement of goods and
works will follow procedures outlined in the Bank's Guidelines for Procurement under IBRD Loans and IDA
Credits, January 1995 (Revised January and August 1996, September 1997, and January 1999) using International
Competitive Bidding (ICB), National Competitive Bidding (NCB) and International or National Shopping
Procedures. Project-financed consultants have been/will be recruited according to the Bank's Guiidelines: Selection
and Employment of Consultants by World Bank Borrowers, Janucary 1977, revised September 1997 and January
1999. Procurement of civil works will be through NCB procedures. Bidding for goods will be packaged to the
extent possible and will be procured as follows: (a) individual contracts estimated to cost US$200,000 or more will
be procured using ICB; (b) individual contracts estimated to cost less than US$200,000 may be procured using NCB.
The aggregate value of such contracts should not exceed US$800,000; and (c) individual purchases of off-the-shelf
items may be procured, through prudent shopping procedures, in packages with an estimated value less than
US$20,000 per contract, up to an aggregate limit ofUS$500,000. Books, journals and other reading materials will
be procured directly Off-the-Shelf or through Subscriptions, up to an aggregate limit of US$50,000. Except for
individuals, all consultants' services have been/will be selected through QCBS procedure method, while auditors will
be appointed through Least-Cost Selection method
Civil Works (US$ 0.38 million): Civil works will comprise site renovation, upgrading of existing facilities in
existing buildings at seven locations of four districts: Dhaka, Chittagong, Benapole, and Mongla, where computer
networking system for the modernization of customs administration will be installed. At Dhaka, computer
networking will be undertaken at four sites - National Board of Revenue (NBR), Dhaka Customs House, Duty
Exemption Drawback Office (DEDO) and the Inland Container Depot (ICD) Terminal under a single contract. The
remaining three sites, Chittagong Customs House, the Benapole Customs House, and the Mongla Custom House are
dispersed in the Districts of Chittagong, Jessore, and Khulna, and as such will be undertaken under three separate
contracts. The amount of each such contract will be small, are unlikely to attract the interest of foreign bidders and,
therefore, will be procured through NCB procedure, acceptable to IDA.
Computer and Computer Networking (USS.63 million): Procurement of Computer Networking System
establishing ASYCUDA++, including their supply and installation to be undertaken under a single contract for
modernization of custom's administration. The networking system will include computers, servers, printers and
network connectivity, and will be procured through ICB procedures. Other personal computers and accessories,
estimated to cost less than US$20,000 per contract may be procured through National Shopping.
Equipment, Vehicles, Furniture (US$1.92 million): Equipment includes modern detection equipment, generators,
vehicles, office equipment (photocopiers, facsimile machines, etc.), training equipment, furniture and air conditioners.



Project Appraisal Document                                                                    Page 67
Country: Bangladesh                                                     Project Title: Export Diversification Project
Except for the modem detection equipment, the individual contracts for other equipment are expected to be small,
costing less than US$200,000 equivalent per contract, and will therefore not be suitable for procurement through ICB
procedure. Contracts estimated to cost US$200,000 equivalent or more (e.g., modem detection equipment estimated
to cost US$1.05 million) will be procured following ICB procedure. Other equipment, vehicles and furniture costing
less than US$200,000 equivalent per contract may be procured through NCB, and those less than US$20,000
equivalenit may be procured following National Shopping procedure (i.e., by soliciting price quotations from at least
three qualified bidders).
Books and Journals (US$0.05 million): Procurement of books and periodicals comprise the bulk of this category,
and will be purchased throughout the life of the project in accordance with the requirements of the executing
agencies. Most of these books and periodicals will be related to protection analysis and trade cooperation in small
quantities and therefore may be procured directly off-the-shelf or through subscriptions.
Consultants' Services and Training (US$17.70 million): Major consultants' services include four contracts, i.e.,
Project Coordinating and Development Unit (PCU), Protection Analysis and Trade Cooperation (PATC), Matching
Grant Facilities Management (MGF), and Customs Administration Modernization (CAM). These were estimated to
cost US$1.50million, US$2.00 million, US$1.95 million and US$4.30 million respectively. Proposals from short-
listed consultants for the services were received and evaluated, and contracts [have been] signed with reputable firms.
Besides, provision of US$ 1.0 million has been kept for new sub-projects that will be identified by the PCU during
early stage of project implementation, and a further US$2.0 million is available for additional subprojects or other
contingencies All the above consultants have been/will be selected using Quality- and Cost-Based Selection (QCBS)
method. Individual consultants required during the implementation of the project will be selected on the basis of
Consultants' qualifications and references. Selection of auditors will be undertaken through Least-Cost Selection
method
Procurement Responsibilities: Procurement responsibilities for works, goods and services will be carried out as
follows:
*  The National Board of Revenue (NBR) will carry out the civil works for the CAM component.
*  Goods for PCU and MGF components will be procured by the Ministry of Commerce (MOC) with the help of
consultants and/or specialists, while the Bangladesh Tariff Commission (BTC) will carry out procurement of
goods for the PATC component NBR will carry out procurement of goods for CAM component.
*  Consultants for PCU, PATC and MGF components [have been] appointed by MOC, while NBR [has] appointed
the consultants for the CAM component.
Acceptability of NCB: The NCB procedures followed by GOB have been reviewed and found to be generally
consistent with the Bank's Procurement Guidelines. hi order to ensure economy, efficiency, transparency and broad
consistency with the provisions of Section 1 of the Guidelines, during negotiations, agreement would be reached with
GOB confirming that the following procedures, irrespective of the value of the contracts, will be adhered to:
(a) invitations to bid shall be advertised in at least one national newspaper with a wide circulation, at least 30 days
prior to the deadline for the submission of bids;
(b) bid documents shall be made available, by mail or in person, to all who are willing to pay the required fee;
(c) foreign bidders shall not be precluded from bidding and no preference of any kind shall be given to national
bidders in the bidding process;
(d) qualification criteria (in case pre-qualification was not carried out) shall be stated in the bidding documents, and,
if a registration process is required, a foreign firm declared as the lowest evaluated bidder shall be given a reasonable
opportunity of registering, without let or hindrance;



Project Appraisal Document                                                                  Page 68
Country: Bangladesh                                                    Project Title: Export Diversification Project
(e) bids shall be opened in public in one location, immediately after the deadline for submission of bids;
(0 bids shall not be rejected merely on the basis of a comparison with an official estimate without the prior
concurrence of IDA;
(g) contracts shall be awarded to the lowest evaluated bidders;
(h) post-bidding negotiations shall not be allowed with the lowest evaluated or any other bidders;
(i) re-bidding shall not be carried out without IDA's prior concurrence;
(j) all bidders/contractors shall provide bid/performance security as indicated in the bidding/
contract documents;
(k) evaluation of bids shall be made in strict adherence to the criteria disclosed in the bidding documents, in a format
and specified period agreed by IDA;
(1) a bidder's Bid Security shall apply only to a specific bid, and a contractor's performance security shall apply
only to the specific contract under which it was furnished;
(m) bids shall not be invited on the basis of percentage premium or discount over the estimated cost;
(n) extension of bid validity shall not be allowed unless justified by exceptional circumstances; and
(o) there shall not be any restrictions on the means of delivery of the bids.
Use of Standard Documents: For ICB procurement of goods, the use of IDA's Standard Bidding Documents
(SBD) is mandatory. For NCB procurement, the implementing agencies (MOC, BTC and NBR) will use the SBDs
for Goods (trial edition August 1997) and Works (trial edition January 1998, Revised February 1999), prepared by
IDA's Dhaka Office (BDO). The Bank's Standard Bid Evaluation Form for Goods and Works (April 1996,
modified by BDO) will be followed for submission of evaluation reports to IDA. For inviting proposals for the four
major consultants' services, the Bank's Standard Request for Proposals (SRFP) forms have been used. Similar form
will be used for inviting proposals for the remaining consultants' services.
Procurement Capacity Review: Procurement capacity of the three implementing agencies (MOC, BTC and NBR)
are varied. NBR has been executing Bank and other donor funded projects and as such there are a core group of
officials who have some expertise on procurement and IDA's Guidelines. However, this capacity is much less in
MOC and BTC. So further training will be required for key procurement staff of MOC, BTC and, to a lesser extent,
the NBR officials.
IDA Prior Review: IDA will carry out the prior review of the first two contracts for the procurement of goods and
the first two contracts for the procurement of works under NCB irrespective of value, and of all goods and works
contracts estimated to cost the equivalent of US$200,000 or more All other contracts will be subject to selective
post-review by IDA. Such selective post-review of contracts below the thresholds will be carried out for
approximately up to five percent of the contracts awarded. The procurement, disbursement and audit team (PDAT)
of IDA's Dhaka Office in Bangladesh or finns hired for the purpose will undertake such reviews of sample contracts.
PDAT will review procedures and discuss its findings with the implementing agencies in order to rectify the
shortcomings identified during the review IDA's prior review will be required for all Services contracts estimated to
cost the equivalent of US$100,000 or more for firrns and US$50,000 for individuals. For all other consultants'
services, IDA will review the terms of reference



Project Appraisal Document                                                                    Page 69
Country: Bangladesh                                                     Project Title: Export Diversification Project
Review of Procurement Process: The progress of procurement will be reviewed as part of the mid-term review of
the project. The compliance with the requirements of different procurement methods and performance standards will
be closely assessed. Based on the review, IDA may revise the prior review threshold including the procurement
methods.
B. Financial ManaLerent Arrangerents and Disbursements
An assessment of the financial management (FM) system of the project was carried out during the preparation stage
of the project, to ensure that the arrangement meet IDA's requirement under OP/BP 10.02 and Guidelines under the
new Loan Administration Change Initiative (LACI). The PCU being outside the ambit of existing Ministry set up,
the FM review and analysis was less complex to undertake. The PCU will coordinate with different agencies and
stakeholders participating in the implementation of the project for reliable and timely preparation of FM reports. A
Finance Cell has been created in the PCU to prepare the consolidated financial statement for the project. It will
maintain consolidated accounts for all project expenditures and receipts on which annual audits will be conducted.
Initially the accounting records will be maintained manually till full migration to the computerized system. A
computerized FM system will be established witlin six months of credit effectiveness. Key aspects of the FM
system are as follows:
Staffing: To make the project LACI-compliant, IDA and GOB agreed to provide a strong FM cell within the project
set-up. Since it would be difficult to mobilize professionally qualified FM personnel from the existing set-up of the
Ministry of Commerce or National Board of Re.venue or from any other implementing agencies, GOB agreed to
provide one long term FM Specialist (FMS) and an Accounts Officer (AO) in the set-up of the project. The FMS
and the AO will be responsible for assisting the project for managing the accounting, FM and disbursement
finctions. The FMS and the AO will act as the nucleus of disbursing all funds and maintaining and preserving all
FM records. An organogram showing the requirements of the staff in the Finance Cell together with their
qualifications and Job descriptions were discussed and agreed with the Ministry of Commerce and included in the
PIP. The provision for FMS and the AO has been included in the PCU consultancy component. The signing of the
consultancy contracts being a condition for Board presentation, both FMS and the AO [have been] appointed through
the PCU consultancy.
Accounting: The financial records of the project will be kept in accordance with generally accepted accounting
principles and practices. While accounts will be kept on a cash basis (following GOB practice), outstanding
expenditures will be accounted for review at least annually and reflected in the Project Balance Sheet. BDXDP shall
establish procedures and records adequate to monitor progress of the project in accordance with sound accounting
practices. The accounting structure reflect the relevant chart of accounts broken down into the types of expenditure
by project component and reflected in the PIP. Initially, the accounts will be manually prepared until the
computerized accounting system is made fully operational and concerned persoinel are trained to run the system.
The project will maintain activity-based subsidiary record for monitoring of detail accounts/key indicators. Both in
manual system and computerized system, the project books of accounts be kept up to date on a daily basis.
Internal Controls: Internal control system covering staffing plan, proper segregation of duties and defined
responsibilities, methods adopted to safeguard project resources and sound policies, procedures and guidelines to
achieve project goals and objectives will be installed in the PCU and also in the sub-projects. PCU's organization
plan showing the functional/reporting relationship among units including Finance Cell is given in the PIP and is
satisfactory to IDA.
Budgeting: There will be proper arrangements and procedures for financial planning, the mechanism for
formulating project budgets and consistency of budgets with FM reporting requirements, and the remedial action it
will take after monitoring reports. The PCU will submit a yearly budget of the project in line with GOB Annual
Development Program to IDA by February for the following financial year taking into consideration of the physical



Project Appraisal Document                                                                 Page 70
Country: Bangladesh                                                   Project Title: Export Diversification Project
work implementation plan of the project for the coming year Such budget will be divided into four quarters as much
as practicable.
Reporting System: The project will prepare quarterly Project Monitoring Reports (PMRs) as per specific formats
discussed and agreed by GOB and included in the PIP. PMR will show:
*  financial statements that include: Sources and Uses of Funds for each quarter, year to-date; and cumulative costs
of project to-date; Usage of funds by Project Activities, Project Balance Sheet; Cash Withdrawal; Cash Forecast;
and a Special Account Statement,
*  Project Progress : Output Monitoring Reports; and
*  Procurement Monitoring Reports
If the PMRs are not submitted within 45 days from the end of the quarter, the disbursement for the next quarter will
be delayed.
Audit Requirements and Arrangements: IDA requires audited financial statement in accordance with intemational
standards on auditing within six months after the end of each fiscal year A private firm of Chartered Accountants
acceptable to the IDA will be used to conduct the audit of the Project Accounts, Special Accounts, and procurement
documentation The audit will undertake a thorough inventory and physical verification of assets procured under the
project. The firm to be selected to conduct the audit will engage a multi-disciplinary team of experts in addition to
audit experts to conduct such audit. Necessary budget provision is made to finance the cost of the audit. The audit
will cover the quality of the work completed besides the above points. The auditor(s) so appointed must be the
Member of the Institute of Chartered Accountants of Bangladesh holding a practice certificate and having affiliation
with an internationally reputed audit firm. The detailed TOR of the auditor have been agreed with GOB and included
in the PIP. The auditor will be appointed within three months from the date of the credit effectiveness. Besides the
above, it is agreed that the Office of the Comptroller and Auditor General will conduct the audit of the accounts of
the project to see that the GOB rules and regulations are complied with where applicable
Project Audit Committee (PAC): GOB agreed to establish a seven-member Project Audit Committee (PAC). The
members of the PAC comprise the president pro tem of the Institute of Chartered Accountants, nominees of the 1999
presidents of the Federation of Bangladesh Chambers of Commerce and Industry and Metropolitan and Chittagong
Chambers of Commerce and Industry, a representative of the Finance Division at or above the level of deputy
secretary, and the chief accounting officers of the MOC and NBR. The FMS of the Project will act as the Secretary
of the PAC.. The Project Steering Committee may co-opt up to three other persons as members of the PAC. Neither
the PDs nor other Project staff should be members of the PAC. The terms of reference of the PAC has been
discussed, agreed with GOB and included in the PIP
Disbursements: With the above arrangement in place, PMR-based disbursements can begin at the project start up
and the requirements of FM System for the project will be consistent with IDA's operational policy in OP/BP 10.02.
Normally all disbursement will be channeled through the Special Account (SA) under PMR based disbursement. To
facilitate timely payment to the beneficiaries, the Government may open and maintain US Dollar SA in Bangladesh
Bank to make payments of IDA's share of expenditures. The advance will be limited to a maximum of 20% of the
credit amount or US 6.00 million whichever is less. Subject to the above condition, the initial deposit to the SA will
be determined on the basis of cash flow requirement to be submitted and agreed on a quarterly basis. Under PMR-
based disbursements the only supporting documentation submitted to IDA will be the quarterly PMRs. However,
PCU will maintain and preserve all supporting documentation authenticating the expenditures reported in the PMR
and made available for review by the auditors and IDA missions
